PETITION FOR SPECIAL LEAVE TO APPEAL (CRL.)  NO. 11595/2026
[Arising out of impugned final judgment and order dated  08-06-2026
in SCRA(Q) No. 1456/2026 passed by the High Court of Gujarat at
Ahmedabad]
SHAILY KUNAL AGRAWAL                               PETITIONER(S)
                                VERSUS
STATE OF GUJARAT & ANR.                            RESPONDENT(S)
IA No. 182428/2026 - EXEMPTION FROM FILING C/C OF THE IMPUGNED 
JUDGMENT, IA No. 182429/2026 - EXEMPTION FROM FILING O.T.
 
Date : 29-06-2026 This matter was called for hearing today.
CORAM : 
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE R. MAHADEVAN
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE ALOK ARADHE
    (PARTIAL COURT WORKING DAYS BENCH)
For Petitioner(s) :Dr. A.M. Singhvi, Sr. Adv.

For Respondent(s) :Mr. Siddhartha Dave, Sr. Adv.

          UPON hearing the counsel, the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
Heard  learned  senior  counsel  appearing  for  the
parties.
1

--- Page 7 ---
SLP (CRL.) NO. 11595/2026
2. Dr. A.M. Singhvi, learned senior counsel appearing for
the petitioner submits that the petitioner-wife filed an
application under Section 379 read with Section 215 of the
Bharatiya Nagarik Suraksha Sanhita, 2023 1, alleging false
deposition, fabrication of evidence and suppression of
material facts by respondent no.2-husband, and seeking
initiation  of  appropriate  proceedings  against  him.
According to learned senior counsel, the respondent has
made ex facie false statements with a view to concealing
his income and assets, which has a direct and serious
bearing on the petitioner’s claim for maintenance and
adversely affects the administration of justice. It is
contended that Section 379 BNSS (corresponding to Section
340 Cr.P.C) contemplates a preliminary inquiry for the
limited purpose of forming an opinion as to whether it is
expedient in the interests of justice to make a complaint.
It is further submitted that continued deferment of such
inquiry would effectively grant respondent no.2 impunity
for  making  false  statements,  thereby  frustrating  the
administration  of  justice  and  causing  irreparable
prejudice to the petitioner and her sever year old minor
child  by  depriving  them  of  maintenance  and  alimony
commensurate  with  the  respondent’s  true  financial
capacity. Reliance is placed on  Iqbal Singh Marwah v.
1 For short, “BNSS”
2

--- Page 8 ---
SLP (CRL.) NO. 11595/2026
Meenakshi Marwah [(2005) 4 SCC 370]  to contend that the
object of the preliminary inquiry is only to enable the
Court to form an opinion whether it is expedient in the
interests of justice to initiate proceedings. Reliance is
also placed on Rajnish v. Neha and another [(2021) 2 SCC
324] wherein, this Court recognised the mischief of false
disclosures in affidavits of assets and liabilities and
observed that where false statements or misrepresentations
are made, the Court may consider initiation of proceedings
under Section 340 Cr.P.C. as well as contempt proceedings.
It is therefore submitted that both the Family Court and
the High Court erred in postponing consideration of the
application  till  the  stage  of  final  arguments  after
hearing respondent no. 2 extensively, though no such
hearing was warranted at the stage of deciding whether a
preliminary inquiry ought to be initiated.
3. The aforesaid submissions are seriously disputed by
Mr.  Siddhartha  Dave,  learned  Senior  Counsel  for  the
respondent no.2. He seeks to distinguish the decisions
relied upon by the petitioner and submits that the Family
Court  has  rightly  exercised  its  discretion.  Drawing
attention to the impugned order, he submits that the
application under Section 379 BNSS pertained to alleged
false statements made by respondent no. 2 during his
3

--- Page 9 ---
SLP (CRL.) NO. 11595/2026
evidence and contradictory statements made on oath. The
parties  were  heard  on  the  said  application,  written
submissions were also filed and considered by the Family
Court, which thereafter directed that the application
would be decided along with the final adjudication of the
matrimonial proceedings. Thus, according to learned senior
counsel, no separate preliminary inquiry is warranted.
4. Although several legal issues have been urged by the
learned senior counsel appearing for the parties, they
have fairly agreed that an attempt may first be made to
resolve their disputes through mediation. 
5. In view of the consensus arrived at between the
parties, we appoint Hon’ble Mr. Justice M.R. Shah (Retd),
former Judge of this Court, as the Mediator. We request
the learned Mediator to accommodate the matter in his
schedule and make an endeavour to facilitate an amicable
settlement between the parties.
6. The parties shall approach the learned Mediator and
work out the modalities of the mediation. The learned
Mediator shall be at liberty to fix the schedule of the
proceedings,  the  terms  and  conditions  governing  the
mediation, and his remuneration, which shall be borne
4

--- Page 10 ---
SLP (CRL.) NO. 11595/2026
equally by the parties.
7. A copy of this order shall be forthwith forwarded to
the learned Mediator.  
8. List  the  matter  after  receipt  of  the  Mediator’s
report.
9. Till then, further proceedings before the Family Court
shall remain in abeyance.
  (POOJA SHARMA)                                  (AVGV RAMU)
     AR-CUM-PS                                 COURT MASTER (NSH)
5

--- Page 11 ---
SLP (C)  NO. 21647/2026

                   Mr. B Lakshmi Pallesh, Adv.
                   Ms. Gayathri, AOR
                   Mr. Jarnail Singh, Adv.                         
For Respondent(s) : 
R.No.1 in          Mr. Sudhanshu S. Choudhari, Sr. Adv. (Through VC)
SLP(C) 21647/2026
R.Nos. 4 to 12 in  Mr. Sravan Kumar Karanam, AOR
SLP(C) 21647/2026  Mr. Santosh Kumar Yadav, Adv.
          UPON hearing the counsel, the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
Heard learned counsel for the parties.
2. The  learned  senior  counsel  appearing  for  the
petitioners submits that the dispute pertains to the
eligibility of 22 individual shareholder-members to be
included in the voters’ list for the election to the Board
of  Directors  of  the  Aurangabad  District  Central
Co-operative Bank Ltd. for the tenure 2026-2031. It is
contended that Resolution No. 20 approving the induction
as members, the issuance of share certificates dated
29.02.2024, the deposit of the requisite share/admission
amount on 14.03.2024, and their participation in the
Annual General Meeting held on 29.09.2025 establish that
2

--- Page 13 ---
SLP (C)  NO. 21647/2026
their membership stood completed before the relevant cut-
off date. It is further submitted that the objections
raised by respondent no. 1 were politically motivated and
that respondent no. 1 had no locus standi to challenge the
petitioners’ membership.
3. Per  contra,  learned  senior  counsel  appearing  for
respondent no. 1 submits that in terms of Section 27(3A)
of the Maharashtra Co-operative Societies Act, 1960, an
individual member becomes entitled to vote only upon
completion of two years from the date of enrolment and
therefore,  the  members  concerned  ought  to  have  been
enrolled on or before 21.03.2024. It is submitted that the
petitioners had not completed the statutory period of two
years as on the qualifying date and were therefore rightly
excluded from the voters’ list. It is further contended
that the Bank’s Annual Report reflected only 59 individual
members as on 31.03.2024, whereas the draft voters’ list
contained 80 names; that the requisite share / admission
amounts  had  not  been  deposited  along  with  the
applications; and that the membership registers in Forms
‘I’ and ‘J’ recorded the date of admission / payment as
12.04.2024. Learned senior counsel also contends that the
counterfoils of the challans relied upon to establish
remittance of the requisite fee are not genuine. It is
3

--- Page 14 ---
SLP (C)  NO. 21647/2026
therefore,  submitted  that  the  objections  filed  by
respondent no. 1 were rightly accepted by the Election
Officer, which order has been affirmed by the High Court.
While seeking time to file a counter affidavit, learned
senior counsel further submits that the election process
has already commenced and any interim order in favour of
the petitioners would disrupt the election schedule.  
4. Having regard to the rival submissions, the issue as
the date of completion of the petitioners’ membership and
the deposit of the requisite admission / share amount
involves  disputed  questions  of  fact,  which  require
consideration on the basis of the material to be placed
before this court. In the meantime, it is directed that
the election process shall proceed as scheduled. However,
the result of the election shall remain subject to the
outcome of these Special Leave Petitions.
5. List the matters after four weeks. 
6. Respondent No. 1 shall file his counter affidavit, by
then.
  (POOJA SHARMA)                                  (AVGV RAMU)
     AR-CUM-PS                                 COURT MASTER (NSH)

ITEM NO.24               COURT NO.6               SECTION IV-A
               S U P R E M E  C O U R T  O F  I N D I A
                       RECORD OF PROCEEDINGS
Petition(s) for Special Leave to Appeal (C)  No(s).  26187/2024
[Arising out of impugned final judgment and order dated  06-02-2024
in WP No. 104149/2023 passed by the High Court of Karnataka Circuit
Bench at Dharwad]
SHANKAR LAKSHMAN SATYANAIK                         Petitioner(s)
                                VERSUS
THE STATE OF KARNATAKA & ORS.                      Respondent(s)
 
Date : 29-06-2026 This petition was called on for hearing today.
CORAM :  HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE MANMOHAN 
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE K. VINOD CHANDRAN
(PARTIAL COURT WORKING DAYS BENCH)
For Petitioner(s) : Ms. Priyanka Terdal, Adv.
                   Mr. Surender Kumar Gupta, AOR
                   
                   
For Respondent(s) : 
          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
Present Special Leave Petition has been filed
challenging the final judgment and Order dated 06 th
February, 2024 passed in Writ Petition No.104149
of 2023 by the High Court of Karnataka whereby the
writ petition of the Petitioner was dismissed on
the ground that Rule 5 of the Karnataka Civil
Services  (Service  and  Kannada  Language
Examination) Rules, 1974 (hereinafter referred to
1

--- Page 19 ---
as ‘Rules 1974’) provides for deemed passing of
Kannada as main language, second language or an
optional subject in SSLC.  The High Court in the
impugned judgment has held that the Petitioner has
neither passed the SSLC examination nor studied in
the 10th Standard.
Learned counsel for the Petitioner submits
that the High Court failed to appreciate that
Proviso to sub-Rule (1) of Rule 3 of Rules 1974
read  with  Notification  dated  21 st June,  1978
exempts  the  petitioner  from  passing  Kannada
language  examination  as  it  exempts  employees
working in certain Class-3 posts like drivers from
passing  the  Kannada  language  examination.
Consequently, according to him, the Petitioner is
entitled to one additional increment.
A perusal of paper book reveals that  Rule 3
read with the Office Order dated 21 st June, 1978
exempts the holders of certain posts from passing
Kannada language examination for the purpose of
earning ‘normal increment’.  
However,  in  the  present  instance,  the
Petitioner  is  seeking  grant  of  ‘additional
2

--- Page 20 ---
increment’ which is governed by Rule 6 of the said
Rules.   In  Rule  6,  as  was  prevalent  at  the
relevant time, additional increment was to be paid
only to those government servants who had passed
or were deemed to have passed Kannada language
examination. 
Consequently, this Court is of the view that
Rule 3 and Government order dated 21 st June, 1978
deal  with  ‘normal  increment’  and  has  no
application  to  ‘additional  increment’  which  is
governed by Rule 6.  
Since the Petitioner does not fulfil the
condition  precedent  stipulated  in  Rule  6,  the
petitioner  is  not  entitled  to  the  additional
increment.  
Accordingly,  the  present  Special  Leave
Petition is dismissed.
Pending application(s), if any, shall stand
disposed of.
(B. LAKSHMI MANIKYA VALLI)                      (DIVYA BABBAR)
COURT MASTER (SH)                             COURT MASTER (NSH)
3

--- Page 21 ---

CONMT.PET.(C) No. 335/2026 in SLP(C) No. 10443/2025
We have heard the learned counsel appearing for
the  petitioner-wife  and  the  learned  Senior  counsel
appearing for the respondent-husband.
Firstly, the statement made by the learned counsel
appearing for the petitioner-wife in the Special Leave
Petition that the Overseas Citizenship of India Card of
the minor child will be handed over to the respondent-
husband within a period of 10 days  from today, being
the outer limit, stands recorded.
Secondly, the respondent-husband is given liberty
to take the minor child to a destination of his choice
for a period of four weeks immediately thereafter.
Finally, taking note of the grievance expressed by
the learned counsel appearing for the petitioner-wife,
the respondent-husband shall make sure that, at least
thrice a week during which time the respondent-husband
is taking the minor child out of the country, the
facility of interaction of the minor child with the
petitioner-wife  through  video  conferencing  must  be
ensured without fail.
List the matter on 11.08.2026.

petitioner further submits that, if the petitioner is given a

such an application is filed, the High court shall

of the observations made by this Court.

disposed of.

of.

IN THE SUPREME COURT OF INDIA
CRIMINAL EXTRA ORDINARY JURISDICTION
WRIT PETITION(S)(CRIMINAL) NO(S).439 OF 2024
RAKESH KUMAR                                       PETITIONER(S)
                                VERSUS
UNION OF INDIA & ANR.                              RESPONDENT(S)
O R D E R
Present  Writ  Petition  has  been  filed  primarily
challenging the constitutional validity of Section 69 of
the  Central  Goods  and  Services  Tax  Act,  2017  which
empowers GST Officials to arrest the offenders. 
The legal validity of the said provision has been
upheld by a three Judge Bench of this Court in Radhika
Agarwal vs. Union of India & Ors. (2025) 6 SCC 545.
Consequently, the present Writ Petition is disposed
of in terms of the aforesaid judgment of this Court.
Interim order, if any, stands vacated.

    (MANMOHAN)
